### DOC: New Ventures Quarterly Update - Q1-2026
ID: 1w7GFc9LH2PT_M8jjNyX3RI9nZ7IJytqIV_z55AYMtsY
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1w7GFc9LH2PT_M8jjNyX3RI9nZ7IJytqIV_z55AYMtsY/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

Ôªø[Insert Tribe Name] - Q1-2026 Global Central Functions Planning Offsite  

________________





I. New Ventures Executive Summary of Q4-2025 Performance

Mega Alliance: Consumer Mega-Alliance | Tribe Name: New Ventures | Tribe Leads: Daniel Arias, Nikita Gorshkov | Tribe Mission: Incubate, validate, and scale new business ventures beyond HelloFresh's core meal kit offering ‚Äîdelivering premium proteins (Good Chop), human-grade pet food (The Pets Table), holistic wellness supplements (Factor Form), and novel customer experiences (Market Innovation); creating the next generation of growth engines for HelloFresh group across new markets, customers and verticals. 

Q4 Core Deliverable: TPT delivered $2.4M in Net Revenue through the launch of delivery tracking improvements & daily calories editing; delivering $6M incremental cumulative CVA OKR for 2025 in December. Good Chop delivered the C@C experiment, aimed at delivering $4.3M and $1.9M in CVA, contributing 20% to the $10M cumulative CVA target in Q4 alone; the VMS team delivered  cadences and achieving 12,560 gross conversions out of a target of 12,500 by the end of November; the Market Innovation Squad managed to deliver the brand new Shopify Store for Factor Form; unlocking peak scaling for new customers.

II. Deep Dive of Q4-2025 Systemic Blockers

Lack of Multi-Subscription Support: throughout 2025, including Q4, the team consistently experienced blockers (UPM/UPL, C@C, Reactivation, Loyalty, Factor Form S&S) as core systems continue to lack default support of multiple subscriptions on plans, order creation, wallet, vouchers & benefits and pricing etc.; resulting in blockers or delays in releasing new functionality, sometimes for months due to lack of capacity or ability to prioritize. 

Lack of Systemic Support for OTP: OTP orders are not effectively supported across corner cases (e.g. multiple subscription brands/cases) across operations (kSCMx, Katana etc.) and SFMC, resulting in blockers on deploying and scaling OTP-based features (e.g. Factor Form OTP & S&S functionality, Good Chop OTP); furthermore there is still a lack of clarity regarding OTP support for vouchers. 

Lack of Voucher Support Across Multiple Use-Cases: throughout 2025 the subscription flexibility across HFG brands has exploded - sub-brands, multiple subscriptions, plan-types, cross-selling, OTP, subscribe & save and bundle offers, yet the HF voucher engine available is still supporting only a single subscription model exclusively. This blocks further scaling and growth of HFG via the new sales and customer engagement methods. 

Lack of ADR Process & Failed Coverage of Use-Cases: during Q4 two cases appeared where existing business models/features and use cases were not included/considered when developing a new feature architecture: Price Sets & Collections Migration. Price Sets to be enabled were designed in such a way that all of the product categories were expected to be collapsed into a single product category, while for HF this is a feasible solution, for other brands (e.g. TPT) this is a non-starter; furthermore, it‚Äôs unclear of the benefit of removing an already available dimension of flexibility for SKUs; on the Collections deprecation and migration to Categories, while it‚Äôs understandable to migrate to the new system to be more supportive of personalization, collections still offer a cheap way to organize recipes, with no clear benefit provided by the deprecation of a lightweight system. 





III. Key Learnings and Failure Analysis

Mitigation Strategy 1  - Core Capabilities Expansion: The New Ventur

Summary

Alison Ryan described a positive recent trip to New York, highlighting the welcoming Good Chop team, including Seban and Yuri, and the collaborative, "scrappy and mighty" vibe of the space. Ryan shared concerns about future uncertainty due to numerous changes and a feeling of being "homeless" without clarity on long-term team belonging, which Nikita Gorshkov acknowledged and promised updates on program reviews. Ryan, Rasha, and Katrina are scheduled for a product design walkthrough on programs this Thursday, following a working session this afternoon, which Jama is also included in, while Ryan is also having working sessions with Samir regarding Good Chop and Shopify.





Details

Notes Length: Standard

* Trip to New York and Impressions of Good Chop Alison Ryan described their recent trip to New York as fantastic and spoke highly of the Good Chop team, noting that Seban and Yuri were very welcoming. They highlighted having a good rapport with Beatatric and Alex, and particularly enjoyed the collaborative, "scrappy and mighty" vibe of the Good Chop space, which reminded them of the early days of HelloFresh. Ryan recounted a fun off-site day visiting the factory, the meat facility, and a logistics site, and mentioned a humorous experience involving Beatatrice packing a box.

* Challenges and Desire for Team Belonging Alison Ryan expressed optimism but admitted that the numerous changes in 2025 created a lingering sense of uncertainty, and they desired better clarity for the shifts expected in 2026. Ryan noted a specific concern about feeling "homeless" in terms of long-term belonging, stating that they are not officially on the market innovation squad or the Good Chop squad but rather support where needed; they find motivation in being part of a stable team. Nikita Gorshkov acknowledged the active start to the new year and promised to keep Ryan posted on the review of programs.

* Programs Walkthrough and Next Steps Alison Ryan reported that a product design walkthrough on programs, involving themself, Rasha, and Katrina, is scheduled for Thursday, after several delays. Ryan expressed that they are prepared for the content and that they, Rasha, and Katrina will connect this afternoon to ensure the design aspects are well-represented. Jama is also included in this conversation, and Nikita Gorshkov noted that Jama needs to keep things "under control".

* Good Chop and Shopify Updates Regarding the Good Chop and Shopify initiatives, Alison Ryan noted having had a good conversation with Yuri and the team that morning and having working sessions with Samir this week. Nikita Gorshkov mentioned having the latest updates after speaking with Samir and suggested that they should push for recharge despite still pending decisions.

* Nikita Gorshkov will keep Alison Ryan posted on the review on the programs as it comes through.

ÔªøThe Pets Table App v1: Notifications-First MVP

Date: 2025-12-11 Authors: Prateek JajooNikita GorshkovAhmed WagdiDaniel Arias Status: Draft





________________





1. Purpose

The Pets Table (TPT) faces a critical retention challenge: our Average Order Rate (AOR) lags behind competitors like Farmer‚Äôs Dog and Ollie, largely due to the lack of proactive, mobile-first customer engagement. This proposal outlines a low-cost, high-velocity strategy to deploy a TPT native mobile app. By leveraging a "webview-first" architecture (React Native shell + existing  web flows), we can bypass expensive native development to deliver v0 (Web Parity) and v1 (Push Notifications). The core value prop isn't the app interface itself, but the notification channel it unlocks‚Äîdriving customers back to the service for order management and upsells, projected to generate ~$1.5M in annualized incremental revenue.

2. Current State / Problem

"Out of sight, out of mind."





* Lagging AOR: TPT‚Äôs AOR is trailing key competitors who utilize native apps to maintain persistent screen real estate and habituation.

* Reactive vs. Proactive: Our current web-only experience relies on customers remembering to visit our site or opening emails (20-25% open rate). We lack a direct, proactive trigger to prompt timely order management.

* Friction: Logging into a mobile website is high-friction compared to persistent app login, discouraging frequent "snacking" interactions where add-on upsells occur.

3. Strategic Solution

Build "The Notification Vehicle" Instead of a costly, multi-quarter native app build, we propose a Webview-First Hybrid App.





* Strategy: Use the Client Platform‚Äôs new React Native infrastructure to wrap our existing mobile web experience.

* Philosophy: "The app is a notification delivery vehicle with a dashboard face. Everything else is a webview."

* Cost/Speed: Minimizes engineering effort by reusing 90% of existing web code. Focuses native development strictly on the "Unlock" features: Push Notifications and Biometric Login.

Core Experiences: v0 vs v1

Feature

	v0 Scope (POC)

	v1 Scope (The Unlock)

	Goal

	Parity & Presence

	Engagement & Revenue

	Core UI

	Full Webview Wrapper (Pixel-perfect recreation of mobile web)

	Webview + Native Navigation Shell

	Authentication

	Persistent Web Session (Cookie-based)

	Persistent Web Session (Cookie-based)

	Notifications

	None

	Rich Push Notifications (Transactional + Marketing)

	Dashboard

	Web View

	Native "Glanceable" Dashboard (Next Box Date, Status)

	Order Mgmt

	Web View

	Web View (Deep-linked from Notifications)

	Upsell

	Standard Web Flow

	Push-Triggered Upsell (e.g., "Add treats to box shipping tomorrow")

	



Detailed scope sheet: Google Sheet Link

4. Business Impact

Hypothesis: Notifications drive frequency; frequency drives AOR and AOV.

Benchmarks (Weekly TPT Updates)

* Current AOR: Lagging behind key competitors (Farmer's Dog, Ollie).

* Competitor Engagement: Apps drive ~2x session frequency vs. mobile web.

* Push Open Rates: 5-10x higher than Email.

Projected Lift (Annualized)

Lever

	Mechanism

	Conservative Impact

	Revenue Impact

	Order Recovery

	"Last chance to edit" & "Card failure" pushes

	+5% AOR (App Users)

	~$1.1M

	Add-on Upsell

	"New treat" & "Box shipping soon" pushes

	+$2 AOV (App Users)

	~$400K

	Total

	



	



	~$1.5M

	



Assumptions: ~50k Active Subs, 30% App Adoption, $80 Base AOV.

5. Technical Strategy

We will leverage the new HelloFresh Client Platform capabilities to avoid building from scratch.





* Shell: React Native "Container"

... [TRUNCATED: 200 chars omitted to save context] ...

A (HelloFresh's notification infrastructure) and Braze/CRM for campaign management.

* Documentation: Infrastructure Architecture

6. Recommendations

1. Proceed with v0/v1 Strategy: Prioritize the notification unlock over native feature parity to maximize speed to value.

2. Leverage Client Platform: Utilize the existing React Native shell infrastructure to minimize overhead.

3. Launch & Learn: Ship v1 to validate the +5% AOR hypothesis before investing in further native features (v2).





________________

Automatically generated by Gemini on 2025-12-11





Two options for V0: 

1. Maximizing web views and customizing the website to look more like an app, which is the least effort option, 

2. Involves having one core page (the dashboard) built with React Native and the rest as web views.

Webview (V0) Only:

Requirements:

* We need to customize for Mobile: header & footer

   * This is unknown effort to a complicated web setup and shared code

* Customize further as the App store may not be allowed for fully webview app 

* Estimated effort 2-4 weeks for 1 engineer (Conservatively)

   * But if it goes above 2 months, we should see if we can should do react-native directly. 





Cons: 

* Web view performance is usually worse, 

* Extensive customizations, such as changing dashboard appearance, would be harder to implement with web views.

* Eventually, we need to move towards all react native so important to webview work may be redundant 

* (Ahmed) Uncertainty of whether deep links (notifications to a specific in-app location) will work with web views





Webview (V0) + React-native dashboard:

* Prioritize Dashboard features (change delivery, change recipe, see feeding guide) & Add-ons

   * Why? - Better performance and user experience for the critical dashboard page.

* Dependencies:  React native platform architecture up in Q2 - So may not even be possible at launch in Q2. 

   * Ahmed: Sync backwards with the relevant team for updates on the infrastructure timeline.

* Timeline: 4 months, with building potentially starting around mid-Q2.





Questions:

1. Is V0 having any measurable impact? - Without notifications

2. We need a page to push the App installation - Checkout page

### DOC: Creator_Marketplace_MVP_Decision_Document_FINAL.md
ID: 1cRgWztGT-nyaXdNbPF8pfcpa_WIdl-9UQO9aggPiNKY

ÔªøCreator Marketplace: MVP Approach Decision Document

Version: 2.0 (Post-Orthogonal Challenge) Date: 2026-01-06 Author: Nikita Gorshkov (Product) Decision Required By: January 13, 2026 Decision Makers: Ed Boyes, Ian Brooks, Jama Musse Orthogonal Reviewer: Gemini (gemini-3-pro-preview)





________________





Executive Summary

The Creator Marketplace aims to transform HelloFresh into a "Spotify for food" platform where creators sell recipes as shoppable, HelloFresh-fulfilled meal kits. After 9 weeks of discovery and orthogonal challenge, we present two viable MVP approaches with a revised recommendation.





Strategic Alignment: TAM Expansion / New Revenue (HFG 2026 Strategy)





YP Target Recalibration:





* Original: $100,000 Net Revenue by March 31, 2026

* Revised Recommendation: Q1 = MVP launch + pilot validation; Q2 = $100K target

* Rationale: Target was set before discovery validated longer path to creator acquisition





________________





I. Background & Problem Statement

The Inspiration-Execution Gap

Consumers save recipes from social media but rarely cook them due to:





* Ingredient complexity (missing items, portion waste)

* Time to source ingredients

* Recipe quality uncertainty

Creator Pain Points

* Platform dependency (algorithm-driven reach)

* Limited monetization beyond sponsorships

* No direct-to-consumer product offering

HelloFresh Opportunity

* Leverage fulfillment infrastructure for creator recipes

* Attract new customer segment (social-first consumers)

* Differentiate from Instacart/Pinterest partnership (individual ingredients vs. complete kits)





________________





II. Competitive Landscape

Competitor

	Approach

	Strengths

	Weaknesses

	Instacart + Pinterest

	1-click grocery list from recipes

	Existing user base, fast

	Individual items, no kit curation

	Tasty (BuzzFeed)

	Shoppable recipes via Walmart

	Media reach

	Generic ingredients, no fulfillment control

	Whisk (Samsung)

	Recipe aggregation

	Smart home integration

	No direct fulfillment

	HelloFresh (Current)

	In-house recipes only

	Quality control, fulfillment expertise

	No creator content

	



Differentiation: HelloFresh is the only player offering complete, pre-portioned meal kits from creator recipes with guaranteed fulfillment quality.





________________





III. Customer Research Insights (Dec 2025)

Key Findings from 4 Customer Interviews (Connie, Barinder, Shima, Ashley)

Value Proposition Validation:





* Solves menu fatigue (core HF customer pain point)

* Eliminates ingredient waste (buying full bottles for 1 tsp)

* NOT seen as "special occasion" only - strong desire for daily meal rotation





Pricing Expectations:





* Expected price: Comparable to or slightly lower than standard HF kits

* Willingness to pay premium: Minor (+10-15%) for creator collaboration

* Price elasticity ceiling: >30% premium is prohibitive

* Strong preference for one-time purchase (no subscription obligation)





Trust Signals Required:





* "Vetted by HelloFresh" badge is critical (green checkmark)

* Unfiltered ratings/reviews essential for social validation

* Recipe Q&A section for cooking questions





Feature Priorities:





1. "Digital Cookbook" - save/organize recipes

2. Filter by cuisine/diet first, creator second

3. "Follow" favorite creators / "Mute" others

4. Skill level tags (Beginner/Intermediate)

5. QR codes linking to original social videos





Adoption Barriers:





* Videos make recipes look easier than reality

* Subscription fatigue (fear of accidental charges)

* Quality risk i

... [TRUNCATED: 9493 chars omitted to save context] ...

Trigger: If 5+ creators are committed by Jan 10 AND Engineering confirms 4-5 FTE allocation AND Culinary confirms 50-recipe capacity.





________________

________________





XIII. Open Questions for Decision Meeting

1. Creator Recruitment Status: Does Marketing have bandwidth to recruit 3-5 creators by Jan 20?

2. Culinary Capacity: Can we vet 15-25 recipes by end of February?

3. Pricing Model: Market-led (creator sets margin) vs. Tiered cost-plus (HF sets base)?

4. Traffic Strategy: Will creator kits be promoted on HF homepage, or purely via creator social links?

5. Attribution: How will we measure incremental revenue vs. cannibalization of existing customers?

6. Q1 Target Reset: Does leadership accept revised Q1 = validation, Q2 = $100K revenue?

Pattern Analysis: Root Causes Across Q4

After reviewing blockers from October-December 2025, three systemic patterns emerge:

Pattern 1: Payment Infrastructure Fragmentation (P0)

Incidents:





* Good Chop C@C refunds failing for CSC experiment customers (Dec 5-25)

* Payment status sync issues between PSP/PPS and BOB/OWL (Dec 23)

* OTP payment handling complexity across brands





Root Cause: HelloFresh's payment infrastructure was designed for weekly subscription charging at cutoff. New Ventures' C@C and OTP models require immediate charge capture with different refund paths. OWL's "error reporting" tab uses legacy RabbitMQ topics incompatible with new refund methods.





Owner: Payments Platform (Shishir Mishra) / Plans Squad Q4 Resolution: Partial - Bob refunds work; OWL fixes deployed Dec 25 Q1 Mitigation: Dedicated payment architecture review for OTP; monitoring dashboard for C@C refund success rate

ÔªøüöÄ Final: Discovery Insights

HF Creator Marketplace:

Discovery Insights and Initial Recommendations from a Research Lense

Last updated: Jan 7, 2026

Authors:  Annette MvdE (Design & Strategy), Katheryn Eckles (Research & Strategy), 



Table of content:

Executive Summary

Project Setup & Research Approach (ready to review)

The Service Vision: The HelloFresh Recipe Creator Marketplace

The Problem Space

Insights and initial reactions to the concept  (WIP)

Translation into MVP and Vision stage (add)

Risks/Barriers, Next Steps and terminology (WIP)





________________





Executive Summary

What is the "Inspiration-Execution Gap"?

The "Inspiration-Execution Gap" is the friction point where a consumer‚Äôs desire to recreate a meal they saw on social media (Inspiration) fails to translate into a finished dish on the dinner table (Execution). While 77% of consumers try recipes they find online, most "saved" videos are never cooked because the path from the screen to the stove is too difficult. This gap is composed of three primary barriers:

* The Logistics Barrier: Unlike buying a shirt or a lipstick, a recipe requires 10‚Äì15 distinct variables (ingredients) to be sourced simultaneously. If even one "niche" ingredient is missing or too expensive, the execution fails.

* The Operational Barrier: To bridge this gap alone, a consumer must manually transcribe a fast-paced video into a shopping list, navigate a grocery store, and manage food waste from buying full-sized packs of unique ingredients. We already see solutions like Instacart providing shoppable links for creators in order to bridge the gap.

* The Trust Barrier: Consumers often doubt if their "execution" will match the "inspiration." Without vetted instructions or pre-measured ingredients, the risk of a "recipe fail" prevents them from starting.





1. Vision for the ‚ÄúHelloFresh Recipe Creator Marketplace‚Äù

Bridge the "inspiration-execution gap" by becoming the premier platform for turning social media content into home-cooked reality. The marketplace focuses on trust, automation, and convenience, offering a low-friction bridge between creator inspiration and HelloFresh fulfillment.

   1. Partner Experience (The Creator Ecosystem)

   1. Operational Ease: Streamlined onboarding using AI-driven automation (URL scraping and nutrition auto-calc) to eliminate creator "operational overload."

   2. Risk-Managed Growth: A hybrid compensation model (Base + Commission) designed to attract high-quality talent despite algorithm volatility.

   3. Brand Protection: Integrated recipe vetting and IP safeguards, ensuring creator reputations are enhanced by HelloFresh‚Äôs quality standards.



      2. Customer Experience (The Cooking Solution)

      1. Frictionless Sourcing: One-click access to niche ingredients and pre-measured portions, solving the cost and waste barriers of social-led cooking.

      2. Utility-Led Discovery: A food-first search engine (by ingredient/cuisine) that prioritizes recipe feasibility and visual clarity over influencer status.

      3. Flexible Access (No-Commitment):

      * On-Demand Purchases: Single-order marketplace functionality for special occasions and weekends without subscription requirements.

      * Smart Scheduling: In-app recipe management and prompts to ensure "saved" recipes are converted into "cooked" meals.



         2. Validated Creators enthusiasm

         1. Methodology: Eleven 60 minute, moderated interviews with social media creators and cookbook authors from the US and Canada. Interviews were conducted in two phases:

### DOC: PRD: Beam Integration for The Pets Table

ÔªøBeam Integration for The Pets Table

________________









Beam Integration for The Pets Table

	Summary: Beam is a social impact integration platform that enables companies to donate a percentage of a customer's purchase to a charity. Instead of the company choosing the cause, Beam allows the user to select the specific charity they want to support from a curated list. 

The Pets Table plans to launch Beam as a conversion rate improvement tool and retention booster. 

	Created At: Dec 19, 2025

	Last Updated: Jan 5, 2026

	Editor(s): Maria Chelminska

	Strategy: xxx

	Figma: link

	Business Scoping Doc / Other documentation: link

	Context

User Problem

As a pet food subscription user, I am struggling with: 

* Choice Overload: Pet food subscription users are faced with a vast number of choices regarding food types and producers, making it difficult to decide which specific brand to commit to.

* Lack of Purpose: Customers are looking for additional reasons or a sense of purpose when choosing a producer; they often feel "powerless" to make a real difference and want their "consumer power" to result in tangible social impact

Vision

By integrating with Beam, we want to transform the decision to subscribe to The Pets Table into a more emotional experience by providing users with a clear purpose. By allowing customers to choose a high-impact nonprofit to support at no extra cost, the brand shifts the relationship from a standard transaction to a mission-driven partnership

Success Metrics:

* Gross CVR improvement (define the breakeven?) [a]

* AOR improvement

* CVA improvement

Scope

V1 Focus: For the initial version, the integration will be limited to the conversion funnel.

* Excluded Elements: V1 will not include the active experience component (the post-purchase subscriber dashboard in settings, impact tracking or cancellation deflection components).

* Included funnel Touchpoints:

   * Early Funnel Teasers: Informing users about the donation option during the quiz, meal selection, or registration steps.

      * Message will be shown on the 2nd question in the quiz (and shown after sex is selected). For multipet users we will no longer show the multipet message on this question. This Message will be implemented from TPT‚Äôs side, independent from Beam API.[b]

   * Charity opt-in and selection on plan selection::[c][d][e] The primary interaction point where the user selects a curated charity. 

      * The optimal placement of the element will be /plans-selection page. This placement will assure early exposure of this benefit[f]

      * We also considered /checkout/payment step, however this page will be to late in the funnel 

* V2 (if experiment is successful)

   * API integration in order to automate data sharing between TPT and Beam and automate donation transfers. 

   * TBD: Sharing IP address to be able to geolocate charities to a consumer‚Äôs location[g]





Iteration ideas (in case V1 turns out to be not as successful as expected)

Risks / Hypothesis: Prospects on plans page are prone to high cognitive load, adding an additional task (choosing a charity) might cause analysis paralysis and hinder conversion rate. 

Solution: Launch, observe and act if needed. Options:

* Changing the placement of the charity selection component (from plans page to‚Ä¶)

   * Registration 

   * Checkout 

* Changing the format of the component (from a popup below the plans, right above the CTA to..)

   * Popup triggered on click, below the plan card which was selected[h] 

* Adding a 2nd entry point for charity selection (plans plus

... [TRUNCATED: 2391 chars omitted to save context] ...

 Cart total

* Order ID

* Zipcode (might not be needed as have IP but zipcode is more reliable)

 

Open Questions: 

1. What are the available charities you support? How should we design the list? Should we go beyond ‚Äúfood for dogs‚Äù and support also clinics / vets? What are the options?

   1. TPT predefined charity - e.g. shelters for dogs in NYC (HQ) 

   2. Local shelter

   3. State-level dog charity (based on API) 

   4. International, high credibility 

2. What are your learnings from long funnels? What is in your opinion the best placement for the funnel?

3. Additional ideas: Have you ever tested a Thank you message (sth like ‚Äúthank you for your contribution‚Äù)? 

4. What are the best copywriting insights you have?

5. How important is ensuring that the donations will be made for every order, until the user cancels? 

6. Legal - do you have an example of T&Cs? Where are T&Cs placed? 

7. Who is responsible for designs? What is the split of ownership? 

8. Any limitations we should be aware of given limiting the experiment to the funnel only? (the semi-manual solution?

2026 HelloTech Tribe Quarterly Planning Update  Template (2-pager)

[Please copy this template, read the guidelines, and then delete this page so that this template is not overwritten.]

Document Guidelines:





These guidelines mirror the structure and clarity of the Yearly Plan documentation to ensure the Tribe's 2-Pager is treated as a serious, strategic planning document focused on cross-functional alignment.





1. What is the purpose of this document? The Quarterly Tribe-Level Update document is intended to surface systemic friction points encountered in the previous quarter and to cascade the Tribe‚Äôs most critical goals and to Central Functions and other Alliances. It summarizes the Tribe's tactical priorities and explicitly calls out cross-functional commitments required for successful Q1-2026 execution.

2. Who owns this document? The 2-Pager document is owned by the respective Tribe Lead. The Tribe Lead is responsible for ensuring the content accurately reflects their Tribe‚Äôs performance, technical reality, strategic intent, and required external commitments.

3. How long do you expect the Tribe-Level update document to be? The Tribe Q4-2025 Review and Q1-2026 Alignment document, including all mandatory sections, must be no longer than two (2) full pages. No appendices are permitted. The document must be immediately scannable and digestible by senior leadership.

4. What are the mandatory sections? All sections detailed in the template are mandatory and must be answered concisely.

5. What is the deadline for submission of the Market Yearly Plans? The Friday prior to the start of the Quarterly Planning Offsite

6. How to submit my Plan Document?  Your Yearly Plan Document must be sent via email by the Tribe Lead to Brian Leung, who will add it to the formal Quarterly Planning Offsite so that all participants can read them prior to the sessions. You can also add the link to your document into tab 3 of the agenda file here.

üí° Guidance  ,,,

### DOC: Influencer Interview Recaps
ID: 1wmE_G1zfRQnwYP4h2ecHxHk7DjI2eTrtTVpRsxmzjrA
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1wmE_G1zfRQnwYP4h2ecHxHk7DjI2eTrtTVpRsxmzjrA/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøInterview: Cheatdayeats

Influencer: Jessica Hirsch of Cheatdayeats

Main Socials: Instagram, Tiktok

Following Size: Instagram 559K, Tiktok: 114K

Content focus: Comfort food with with interesting twists and formats

Interview Date: Nov. 14, 2025

Part 1: Creator Background

* Primary Goal: Her main goal is building a strong community and establishing trust with her followers. She wants her content to be accessible, fun, and easy, focusing on recipes that are not overly complex (e.g., 5 ingredients, 15 minutes).

* Content & Platforms: Her content has evolved from featuring restaurants to focusing on her own recipes.

   * Her main platforms are Instagram and TikTok, but she is also building on YouTube, Facebook, and Threads.

   * She noted that her Instagram audience feels more like a "hardcore" community, while TikTok feels more random and driven by the "For You" page.

   * She tailors content, finding that TikTok performs better with longer, descriptive videos, whereas Instagram favors short, quick videos.

* Workflow & Tools: She works as a two-person team with her husband. He assists with filming and emails, while she handles most of the editing and community engagement. She uses Capcut and Premiere Pro for editing.

* Monetization: Her income is primarily from brand deals and creating UGC (User-Generated Content) for brands. She makes some money from the TikTok fund but finds the monetization rules across platforms to be confusing and hard to keep up with.

* Biggest Challenges:

   * The Algorithm: Her single biggest challenge is connecting with her audience due to the "ebb and flow" of platform algorithms. She struggles to know if low engagement is due to her content or the algorithm simply not showing it to her followers.

   * Time & Trends: As a small team, she finds it challenging to be consistent and invest time across all platforms. If she could delegate one task, it would be keeping up with all the different platform-specific trends, audios, and algorithm changes.

________________





Part 2: The HelloFresh Concept & Feedback

Value Proposition

* Her initial concern was cost and timeliness versus just using Instacart.

* However, she quickly saw the value in providing exact, pre-portioned ingredients, noting she has also bought an expensive spice just to use it once.

* She felt the concept would be especially powerful for recipes involving unique, expensive, or hard-to-find ingredients, like pistachio paste for the viral Dubai chocolate trend.

Ingredient Strategy & Value

The core value for users will come from the ingredients. Jessica stressed that the program must:

* Focus on Unique/Specialty Items: The program's biggest draw would be providing ingredients that are hard to find, expensive, or unique. This creates a clear value-add over a user just going to their local supermarket.

* Highlight Pre-Portioned Savings: The program should emphasize the value of providing exact portions of expensive ingredients (like saffron or pistachio paste) so the user doesn't have to buy a large, costly jar for a single recipe.

* Ensure High-Quality Ingredients: Jessica was very clear that the quality of the ingredients is critical. She noted that for recipes with few ingredients, the quality matters a lot (e.g., "which sharp cheddar" is being used).

Creator-Follower Connection

The program must be designed to enhance, not just use, the creator's existing community.

* Create a "Full Circle" Loop: Jessica suggested including a QR code or link in the box that directs the user back to the creator's original post, website, or

New Ventures Operational Overhead calculation



"How it works

This sheet provides the percentage of operational overhead (i.e. KTLO work per month). Each team has a dedicated tab. For this to work, you need to
* add the label KTLO to all Jira tickets that you consider KTLO work
* Make sure all tickets that move into the ‚Äúresolved‚Äù state have assigned story points. Add the actual story point in hindsight for accurate operational overhead calculation
A cron job runs every night and updates this sheet. It used the resolved date to include a ticket in the calculation for a specific month.
"

### DOC: Flexible Hybrid Policy_USA
ID: 1FKqBn4Ccl_XZmkLz8gRg4nNe5AfEXQpXHyLEU_xVHqQ
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1FKqBn4Ccl_XZmkLz8gRg4nNe5AfEXQpXHyLEU_xVHqQ/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøContinuing our Commitment to the Flexible Hybrid Policy

We‚Äôve demonstrated that we don‚Äôt need to be in the office everyday to remain productive, but we continue to believe that an increased level of in-person interaction is important to fostering a positive and effective culture ‚Äì an environment where you‚Äôre able to make connections, collaborate and build skills to help you elevate your career.





Our flexible hybrid policy requires your in-office time to be equivalent to 50% of your time (or an average of 2.5 days a week). In practice, this is a minimum of two days one week, three days the opposite, which provides you with the flexibility to choose whether you want to be in the office or work remotely for the other part of your workweek. This is a balance we are confident fosters productivity, collaboration and employee satisfaction.

Who is Eligible?  

All non-essential in-workplace employees based in our U.S. HQ or DC locations (NYC, Boulder, Mulberry, Chicago and Brooklyn studio). For anyone on a schedule other than 5x8s, the expectation is that you come in 50% of the time. For example, flex hybrid employees working 4x10s are expected to be in 2 days per week. Please consult with your HRBP if you are unsure about whether the flexible hybrid policy applies to you.

How Does the Flexible Hybrid Policy Work?

The HelloFresh flexible hybrid is a policy that promotes a level of in-person interaction with your colleagues while also allowing you the flexibility to choose a workplace schedule that best supports your work/life balance and productivity.









	Flexible Hybrid Guidelines

	



	In The Office

	You

	Your Team

	New Hires + Manager

	You

	Company‚ûï

	Flexible Hybrid in Practice

At a high level, the flexible hybrid policy requires you to be in the office for an average of 2.5 days per week. This is equivalent to 50% of the month, with the expectation that you are rotating each week during the month between 2 and 3 days. 





Additionally, once per month, company days will be scheduled for full office teams to gather. While not required, it is encouraged that you join to help build a stronger, more collaborative office culture. Team days & company days do count toward your requirement. 





For new hires joining the company, the expectation is that you (and your hiring managers) spend the first two weeks immersing yourself in all things HelloFresh at one of our HQ locations.





Below is a more detailed explanation of the policy and what each of the ‚Äòdays‚Äô mean. Note, you are still required to reserve a desk in your respective office through Envoy. Need a refresher? Check out this FAQ document.





Your Days

On rotation, two or three days per week (on days of your choosing), we ask that you come into one of our HQ office locations. Coming to the office helps you stay connected, build camaraderie and encourage collaboration. On these days, you can schedule 1:1s with your manager, collaborate and build camaraderie with your colleagues.





Team Days

At the discretion of team leads and scheduled in advance, employees may be asked to come to the office along with their direct teams to foster connection and collaboration with your closest colleagues. On these days, you‚Äôll likely have team meetings, workshops, project post mortems and other social activities. Note, these days do count toward your 50% in-office requirement.





Company Days

In addition to your days & team days, company days will be scheduled once monthly to bring full office teams together. While not mandatory, we strongly encourage you to join your colleagues in the office to boost morale, build culture and collaborate. On these days, you‚Äôll do things like work cross-functionally, partake in social events and gatherings and join larger full-office or company meetings.





Flex Days

Outside of team and company days, we‚Äôre giving you the flexibility to choose whether you‚Äôd like to come to the office or work from home ‚Äì whichever allows you to be the most productive. You‚Äôve earned our trust and have demonstrated productivity in a hybrid environment so we don‚Äôt want to take that away. Please note, if you choose to work from home, you‚Äôre responsible for ensuring you have the tools & resources you need to be successful.





New Hires & Onboarding

Every new hire will be expected to spend their first two weeks with the company in the office in order to fully immerse themselves in all things HelloFresh; our people, policies and processes. We also want to ensure you‚Äôre fully equipped and set up for success as you begin your employee journey. Your manager (or assigned proxy) will also be expected to join you in the office for these 2 weeks, and others on your team may be asked to come in as part of your onboarding, too. 





If you have any questions, please view the comprehensive FAQ or open a ticket here using the Case Type = 'US - Hybrid Work/Return to Office'.

ÔªøFinal SOLUTION (WIP)

HelloFresh NL Premium Tier & Green Chef Migration - Solution Design Review





 Author(s): Vimal GargJolanta CariovaJo√£o Cheffer Prado

Last Update: Sep 25, 2025

Status: Draft | In Review | Final

Project Overview

This project consists of two sequential phases:

* M1: Green Chef NL to HelloFresh NL Migration

* M2: Premium Tier A/B Test for HelloFresh NL, BE & LU Active Customers

Key Questions

#

	Question

	Answer

	1

	How do we ensure seamless credential transition without requiring customers to create new passwords?

	We won‚Äôt reuse auth tokens. Customers will receive a magic link (or similar one-time login) to activate their new HelloFresh NL account, avoiding password creation at migration) however, they would still need to reset their password in case they log out from HF NL again since we cannot migrate password. We could support this with a clear password reset flow alongside the magic link.[a][b][c][d][e][f]

	2

	What's our approach for handling customers with existing HelloFresh accounts?[g]

	We could attach Premium Tier product-family to existing HF accounts with the same email instead of creating duplicates. This is technically feasible but would depend on a product (and legal) decision before implementation. All we need to do is basically changing their subscription plan to the newly created product-family for the premium tier.

Jo√£o Cheffer Prado

	4

	What's the rollback plan if migration issues occur during W7 2026 delivery window?

	Customers would remain active on Green Chef, so rollback is essentially stopping the migration[h][i] job or just basically delete the ‚Äúduplicated‚Äù account on HF NL or either require confirmation by email to validate before activation. Exact flow should be aligned with Product, but technically all options are possible.

	5

	How do we handle GDPR compliance[j] during the data migration process?

	Customer data is duplicated only for active NL customers with clear business purpose (service continuity) such as addresses and the payment token. Migration will follow GDPR principles: purpose limitation, data minimization (no historical orders[k][l][m]), audit trail, and secure handling in staging/production)

	6

	Green Chef Migration - Legal & Customer Segmentation?

* Can we migrate all active GC customers to Premium, or do we need consent-based opt-in due to BNL legal sensitivities?[n]

* How do we handle vegan/vegetarian customers where HF doesn't offer comparable options? (potential breach of dietary commitments)[o]

	



	7

	Pricing & Customer List Ownership

* MISSING: List of "high value" GC customers to be migrated[p] (who provides this list?)

	



	8

	Migration

* Cash credits / Hellocredit[q][r][s] migration approach - confirmed?

	



	9

	Preferences (to check with Katrien Oosterom) 

-  Can we have multiple different premium preferences (e.g., "Classic Premium" and "Healthy Premium")?

- any other challenges on preferences?[t]

	



	10

	Elysium[u] Dependencies & implications on timelines

- Jolanta Cariovato check if UX needs adjustments[v][w]

	



	11

	Experiment Allocation & Segmentation

* CDP or Statsig?

	



	12

	Data & Analytics

Tere Ledesma to define use cases and secure validation from the tech team. 





	



	13

	Technical[x] handover 

1. Jo√£o Cheffer Pradoto cover how migration can work (POC done in the past[y][z][aa][ab])

2. Any other details on UX estimation /solution design

	



	



1. Summary of the Project

Business Case: BNL Mosaic Price & Margin modelling - Scenarios Comparison[ac]

Project Structure: Two-Milestones A

### DOC: KN - Reset To Trial Customers
ID: 1Ii2Oj1Kqa17eyF9htI-jT86mA3bivy_sJKVjgM227ek
Link: https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1Ii2Oj1Kqa17eyF9htI-jT86mA3bivy_sJKVjgM227ek/edit?usp=drivesdk

,,,,,,,,,,,,,

,Purpose: ,,,,,,,,,,,,QUERY  into databricks

,,"New TPT customers who sign up are entitled to a ""Trial"" Box which is smaller in size and lower in price. Due to payment errors or CC/Logistics issues, trial boxes may get canceled. We need to send subscriptions who had their trial box cancelled due to payment error for the New Ventures Tech team to manually ""reset"" subscriptions back to the ""trial"" sku so that this price can be honored on the second box. Once a trial box has been reset for over 4 weeks and customer still has a failed payment, we want to cancel the subscription to avoid further weekly order creations.",,,,,,,,,,,WITH CanceledOrders AS (

,,,,,,,,,,,,,SELECT

,,,,,,,,,,,,,"subscription_id,"

,,,,,,,,,,,,,"customer_id,"

,,,,,,,,,,,,,COUNT(order_nr) AS total_canceled_orders

,,,,,,,,,,,,,FROM

,,,,,,,,,,,,,payments_hf.f_orders fo

,Standard of Procedure,,,,,,,,,,,,WHERE

,,,,,,,,,,,,,country = 'KN'

,1,"UPDATE QUERY to make sure hellofresh_delivery_week is CURRENT WEEK and delivery_date is after TODAY's date; Create a new tab in this sheet (i.e. ""2025_W49"")",,,,,,,,,,,"AND latest_status IN ('canceled', 'clarify_payment_error')"

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND box_shipped = 0

,2,"From the query results, cancel subscriptions where ""total_canceled_orders = 5+ cancelled orders"" using reason = ""CC-Failed-Payments"" and then delete from list.",,,,,,,,,,,AND product_type = 'mealbox'

,,Cancel subscriptions either individually or using bulk function on BOB,,,,,,,,,,,GROUP BY

,,,Using BOB bulk function:,,,,,,,,,,"fo.subscription_id, fo.customer_id"

,,,Create a CSV with the following headers: ,,,,,,,,,,)

,,,,id,customer_id,reason,,,,,,,SELECT DISTINCT

,,,,,,CC-Failed-Payments,,,,,,,"fo.subscription_id,"

,,,"Upload CSV file using BOB > Bulk > Import > New > Click ""Browse"" to select file > Under Operation, select ""Subscription Cancel"" > Validate > Click New again > Upload",,,,,,,,,,"fo.customer_id,"

,,,,,,,,,,,,,"soi.sku,"

,3,"In the ""CC KN Reset"" tab, look for new entries from CC (lines without WEEKNUM function), and amend these subscriptions to new tab (i.e. ""W10"")",,,,,,,,,,,fo.delivery_date

,,,"before sending these to the NV Squad team, separate the current (today) and future (tomorrow)'s delivery dates. CC KN resets to a different column.  ",,,,,,,,,,",CASE"

,4,"Send a question via slack #squad-nv-pet-food, to have an engineer pick up this task. ",,,,,,,,,,,WHEN co.total_canceled_orders >= 5 THEN '5+ boxes cancelled'

,,,type in /new_issue,,,,,,,,,,ELSE co.total_canceled_orders

,,,Yes I want to create a new issue,,,,,,,,,,

,,,Issue Title: ,Reset subscriptions to trial,,,,,,,,,

,,,Select topic: Other,,,,,,,,,,END AS total_canceled_orders

,,,Priority:, High,,,,,,,,,from payments_hf.f_orders fo

,,,Description: subscription_ids found in column A of this spreadsheet Week # <Paste link>,,,,,,,,,,LEFT JOIN canceledorders co ON fo.subscription_id = co.subscription_id

,,,Expected Behaviour:,Reset trial to subscription,,,,,,,,,LEFT JOIN dl_bob_live_non_pii.sales_order_item soi ON fo.subscription_id = soi.fk_subscription AND fo.country = soi.business_unit

,Schedule,,Actual Behaviour,Payment errors,,,,,,,,,LEFT JOIN dimensions.product_dimension pd ON soi.sku = pd.product_sku AND soi.business_unit = pd.country

,,"On Tuesday, we want to take the delivery_dates from Saturday to Tuesday (e.g. On Nov 25, 2025, we want to delivery_dates 2025-11-22 to 2025-11-25)",,,,,,,,,,,LEFT JOIN dl_bob_live_non_pii.subscription s ON soi.fk_subscription = s.id_subscription AND soi.business_unit = s.business_unit

,,"On Friday, we want to take the previous delivery_dates from Wednesday to Friday (e.g. On Nov 28, we want delivery_dates 2025-11-26 to 2025-11-28)",,,,,,,,,,,where fo.country = 'KN'

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND customer_loyalty = 0

,,,,,,,,,,,,,"AND latest_status NOT IN ('shipped','money_received')"

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND fo.box_shipped = 0

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND hellofresh_delivery_week >= '2025-W48' --update to current week

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND fo.delivery_date <= '2025-11-25' --update to today's date +1 day

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND fo.dunning_decision = 'cancel'

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND fo.product_type = 'mealbox'

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND pd.is_trialbox IS TRUE

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND soi.sku LIKE 'KN-T%'

,,,,,,,,,,,,,AND s.canceled_at IS NULL

,,,,,,,,,,,,,ORDER BY

,,,,,,,,,,,,,total_canceled_orders DESC;

### DOC: DRAFT - Good Chop - Shopify Storefront
ID: 1cRsj8ii021Sb1NY-FEnjlbV9NtW05ItT8lJzdakP-DQ
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1cRsj8ii021Sb1NY-FEnjlbV9NtW05ItT8lJzdakP-DQ/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

Ôªøüöß Overview





Good Chop - Shopify Storefront

	Created At: Oct 27, 2025

	Last Updated: Jan 6, 2026

	Status: In Progress

	Authors: Alison Ryan Sameer Doda

	



Summary[a][b]

This document outlines the approach and implementation strategy for launching a Shopify storefront for Good Chop. It is organized into three phases, with each section detailing the goals, scope, and execution for that phase.

The primary objective is to launch an independent storefront that enables Good Chop customers to order products with greater flexibility. This initiative will help us assess how a standalone channel impacts ordering behavior, customer lifetime value, and product adoption, while also evaluating the operational effort and cost-effectiveness of this approach.

Strategy Review





Objective: Launch a standalone, item-based e-commerce storefront to establish baseline performance metrics and validate the demand for a non-subscription model.



What is the problem we‚Äôre trying to solve? Currently, our technical architecture restricts us to a subscription-only model. This creates a high-friction entry point for new users. We lack a traditional e-commerce "marketplace" experience where customers can browse the full Good Chop catalog and view item-based pricing before committing to an account or subscription.



What is the solution? We will launch a Shopify-driven storefront that enables a one-time purchase experience. This new experience empowers customers to either buy individual products in their desired quantity or create a custom box, which will require a minimum order value (dynamic bundling). This approach grants customers complete control over their selections without obligating them to a recurring subscription plan.



Who is the target customer? 

* New Customers: High-intent shoppers specifically seeking certain proteins who prefer a one-time purchase over a recurring subscription.

* Existing Good Chop Customers: Customers who need a quick, low-friction way to make an one-off purchase  purchase (e.g., for a special event) independent of their regular subscription.

* Former Good Chop Customers: Customers who value the product but want a commitment-free way to purchase. Desire to purchase as needed without a recurring subscription's overhead.

What is the target customer experience? 

* Discovery: Users clicking on targeted ads or searching for specific cuts (e.g., "Filet Mignon" or "Wild-caught Salmon") will be directed to the Shopify storefront.

* Conversion: Customers can explore the item-based menu, add products to their cart, and select a preferred delivery date.

* Checkout: Users can complete their purchase via guest checkout or by creating an account.

* Retention: Post-purchase, customers will have the ability to seamlessly reorder their previous "one-time" boxes through their account portal.

Success criteria





Success will be evaluated based on core metrics, including CAC, CVR and AOR. We will also track user journey analysis, CLV and product uptake to identify any performance differences for specific protein cuts in an e-commerce context. The assessment of this new channel will focus on its operational efficiency and cost-effectiveness.

* Product Uptake: The rate and speed at which customers adopt and purchase protein

   * This includes measuring initial trial rates, the percentage of the customer base adding the new item to their orders, and segmenting uptake by new versus existing subscribers.

* Order Habits: The influence of item-based proteins on customer purchasing behavior, including changes in AOV, order fr

... [TRUNCATED: 24697 chars omitted to save context] ...

unch is Q2, pending evaluation of phase 1.

* Phase 3: To be determined, following evaluation of results from Phases 1 and 2.

This new storefront will allow us to quickly gather insights and validate initiatives that are challenging to test within our current technology stack. It will initially focus on targeting customers from specific acquisition channels, such as prospects using SEM to look for particular cuts of meat.

The rapid and streamlined setup of the Shopify marketplace will be managed in partnership with an external team, Anatta.

Phase 1: MVP Marketplace Launch

### DOC: 2026 People Domain Objectives
ID: 1wCEpKV3LSRuUAO_qjkPUuO2mBIPp5_4chdbDjqupRZM
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1wCEpKV3LSRuUAO_qjkPUuO2mBIPp5_4chdbDjqupRZM/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøDomain Objectives

* People Domain 2026





1. Objective: Enable a Reliable, Engaged, and Efficient Front-Line Workforce

Measure of success: Early Attrition Rate (Output Metric) throughout the year we will bring visibility to the adequate input metrics

Objective Owner: Shawn Spanier Philipp B√∂rnerJames Gorman 

Investment Type: Existing 

HFG Top 5 Strategy Impact:  1. Quality, Packaging and Ingredient SKU innovation 2. XL Menu Expansion5. Efficiency Program/Cost to Serve 

Description: Our objective is to ensure our front-line associates are proud to be part of the HelloFresh team by building an engaged, safe, and reliable workforce. We will enhance the employee experience through consistent HR processes, clear manager expectations, and a focus on safety and respect, all of which will directly improve labor efficiency and cost.

1. Scalable people foundation: In line with operations project Highlander we will seek to establish standards related to Field People including defining operational jobs and career progression, staffing footprint based on building type and size, shift schedules, labor planning approach, employee relations and policy frameworks, etc. to facilitate consistent operating models that scale along with our single operational technology stack. We will standardize only where there is a clear benefit in 1) deploying standard processes and tools for labor planning or 2) solving employee pain points that result in expected enhancement in early retention. 

2. Global Workforce Health Mechanism: We will establish and build on mechanisms to review operational healthiness with a consistent focus on the right workforce mix, attrition, absenteeism, and engagement. We will partner with operations to harmonize  weekly reviews and ensure deliberate action is taken to address pain points with the goal of identifying and quickly solving employee and staffing issues with a repeatable feedback loop. 

3. Global Workday Implementation: We will implement FreshField globally to have 100% of workers in our system. This will facilitate improved visibility into our labor availability, enhanced reconciliation for invoicing of contingent labor, and facilitate better communication with employees through engagement feedback loop touchpoints.

















































2. Objective: Enable a high performance culture and increase our talent density

Measure of success: Regrettable Attrition % of HiPo/Critical roles, Achievement of top 3 talent priorities

Objective Owner: Shawna Fehrman-LeeYasar AhmadSyed Ali Abbas

Investment Type: Existing    |  HFG Top 5 Strategy Impact:  All 

Description: This objective is about executing on our existing processes with a renewed and clear focus on business impact. Our HRBPs will work with leaders to have clear talent priorities that enable our top 5 strategies. They will partner with our COEs so that our talent processes and rituals are used as tools to bring those objectives to life.  We will achieve this by setting clear expectations, modeling the right behaviors, and providing data to enable accountability. 





1. Defining & Reporting on Business Talent Objectives: HRBPs will spend the rest of 2026 defining concrete talent objectives and the GLT will implement a quarterly reporting mechanism to show progress versus those initiatives. Example initiatives include: Design the target footprint for the MD organization and transition to that footprint by EOY. Implement a multi-location talent strategy to increase the number of Engineers as a percentage of the total tech team populat

... [TRUNCATED: 7865 chars omitted to save context] ...

 in technology investment. We also experience meaningful spikes in unplanned work that may require us to re-prioritize. Additionally, as an organization we are yet to mature in terms of processes, leadership capability, and ways of working. This creates both opportunity for growth and significant dependency on HR, as managers often lack the skills to independently handle people issues, engagement, and grievance management. While standardisation (systems, tools, processes) offers potential benefits, the organisation may not yet be ready; building managerial and organisational capability is a necessary foundation. Without this, HR will remain overstretched, providing compensatory support instead of enabling a more self-sufficient & independently capable leaders & business.



      * What objectives would MDs and other key stakeholders be most disappointed to have left out for 2026? 

         1. Addressing low Foodie budgets and salary bands which are driving top performer attrition 

         2. Improving specific items in performance management and related processes (i.e. ease performance curve restrictions, have more business leader discretion on allocation of Foodie raises and perf grants, simplify Foodie process further, make it more or less )

### DOC: Creator Marketplace ‚Äî MVP Approach
ID: 1l0pmjbN9M3eWfCyiBgUFeMRLYrK1ogrIHVzvAmM4978
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1l0pmjbN9M3eWfCyiBgUFeMRLYrK1ogrIHVzvAmM4978/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøTab 1

Creator Marketplace ‚Äî MVP Approach

Objective

Align on the MVP approach by deciding how much creator scale is needed to unlock customer demand, while balancing time to market, learning velocity, scalability, and investment risk.

________________





MVP Options Evaluated

Option 1 ‚Äî Customer Portal Only (Manual Creator Onboarding)

Launch the customer-facing marketplace experience only. Creators are onboarded manually; profiles and recipes are created and managed internally.[a]

Advantages

	Risks

	Learnings

	* Fastest time to market

* Lowest engineering and design investment

* Maximum brand, quality, and operational control

* Strong signal on customer demand with minimal risk

	* Not scalable on the creator side

* Limited supply may artificially cap demand

* 	* Raw customer demand, content ‚Üí conversion

	



________________





Option 2 ‚Äî Customer Portal Launch + Immediate Creator Tooling Build

Launch the customer-facing marketplace first, and immediately continue building creator self-serve tooling without waiting for full demand validation. Early customer and operational learnings inform‚Äîbut do not gate‚Äîthe creator portal build.[b]





Advantages

	Risks

	Learnings

	* Faster path to scale than demand-gated approaches

* Maintains momentum and signals strategic intent to creators

* Creator tooling is informed by real usage data, not assumptions

* Reduces long-term operational drag early

* Avoids costly re-platforming later

	* Higher upfront investment than Option 1

* Some risk of building ahead of proof

* Partial rework risk if assumptions change

	* Demand + creator behavior + operational friction

	



________________





Option 3 ‚Äî Full Two-Sided Marketplace Launch

Build and launch customer and creator portals together with full self-serve capabilities from day one.

Advantages

	Risks

	Learnings

	* Fully scalable from launch

* Strong creator acquisition narrative

* Large recipe catalog immediately available

	* Longest time to market

* Highest engineering and opportunity cost

* Requires reprioritizing other MIO initiatives

* Highest risk if demand is weaker than expected[c]

	* Marketplace dynamics at scale (highest risk)

	



________________





Comparative Snapshot





Dimension

	Option 1

	Option 2

	Option 3

	Time to Market

	Low

	Medium

	High

	Demand Validation

	High

	Low

	None

	Creator Scalability

	Low

	Medium‚ÄìHigh

	High

	Upfront Investment

	Low

	Medium

	High

	Brand / Ops Risk

[d]	

Low

	Medium

	High

	



MVP Success Signals (Decision Gates)

* Conversion from creator recipe view ‚Üí order

* % of new customers acquired via creator content

* Repeat purchase behavior

Decision & Sign-Off





Name

	Decision

	Date

	Ed Boyes

	* Option 1

	Jan 13, 2026

	* Option 1

NGO: PMOS Review

Creator Marketplace: MVP Approach Decision Document[e]

Version: 2.0 (Post-Orthogonal Challenge) Date: 2026-01-06 Author: Nikita Gorshkov (Product) Decision Required By: January 13, 2026 Decision Makers: Ed Boyes, Ian Brooks, Jama Musse Orthogonal Reviewer: Gemini (gemini-3-pro-preview)





________________





Executive Summary

The Creator Marketplace aims to transform HelloFresh into a "Spotify for food" platform where creators sell recipes as shoppable, HelloFresh-fulfilled meal kits. After 9 weeks of discovery and orthogonal challenge, we present two viable MVP approaches with a revised recommendation.





Strategic Alignment: TA

... [TRUNCATED: 13222 chars omitted to save context] ...

 Recruitment Status: Does Marketing have bandwidth to recruit 3-5 creators by Jan 20?

2. Culinary Capacity: Can we vet 15-25 recipes by end of February?

3. Pricing Model: Market-led (creator sets margin) vs. Tiered cost-plus (HF sets base)?

4. Traffic Strategy: Will creator kits be promoted on HF homepage, or purely via creator social links?

5. Attribution: How will we measure incremental revenue vs. cannibalization of existing customers?

6. Q1 Target Reset: Does leadership accept revised Q1 = validation, Q2 = $100K revenue?





________________





XIV. Appendix: Orthogonal Challenge Log

Challenger: Gemini (gemini-3-pro-preview) Date: 2026-01-06 Tokens: 13,576 (11,313 prompt, 531 response, 1,732 thoughts)

Challenges Raised:

#

	Section

	Issue

	Resolution

	1

	Exec Summary vs. Recommendation

	Timeline incompatibility with $100K Q1 target

	Reset target: Q1 = validation; Q2 = $100K

	2

	Decision Framework

	Over-engineering for 3-5 creators (Lean MVP violation)

	Repositioned Option A as true Concierge MVP; Option B only with 5+ creators

	3

	Customer Research

	Unvalidated unit economics (price ceiling + creator fees)

	Added margin model analysis showing viability at 15% premium

	4

	Dependencies

	Culinary bottleneck missing from resources

	Added Culinary capacity as gating dependency

	5

	Risks

	Missing traffic/attribution strategy

	Added attribution model to dependencies and open questions

Meeting records Transcript 





Summary

Laurent Guillemain reaffirmed the brand's mission and vision, outlining six core strategic pillars for 2026, which prioritize investing in product with a recipe score target greater than 4.30 and driving the business unit to EBIT profitability by the end of 2027. Daniel Arias and Laurent Guillemain discussed increasing the low recipe rating rate and the team agreed to follow up on optimizing data collection entry points and questions, while Maria Chelminska announced adding new SKUs, including a small 60-calorie air-dried SKU, and Dovas Zakas noted marketing team additions and positive early results from an AI chatbot test. Other key objectives for the year include increasing the multipet conversion rate to over 18%, reducing Fresh and Air-Dried Cost of Goods Sold by 6% and 7.5% respectively, increasing brand awareness from 11% to 16.5%, and expanding the retail business, as evidenced by Walmart's expansion into 655 stores.





Details

Notes Length: Standard

* Mission and Vision Laurent Guillemain reaffirmed the brand's mission to "help pets live a happier, healthier life by changing the way they eat". The vision is to be an omni-channel brand that ensures both pets' and their parents' happiness by offering healthy products with variety, value, and ease of mind (00:00:00). They noted that the vision, created around the end of 2024 or the start of 2025, remains true (00:01:02).

* Six Core Strategic Pillars for 2026 Laurent Guillemain outlined six core strategic pillars for the pet stable, emphasizing the importance of their order. The priorities include investing in product, focusing on retention, driving the business unit to EBIT profitability by the end of 2027, efficiently scaling the business for greater than 110 million Annual Run Rate (ARR), building out the retail business line to over 12 million ARR with strong profit contribution, and maintaining a high-performing team. The key performance indicator (KPI) for product investment is a recipe score greater than 4.30 across three dog food formats (00:01:02) (00:03:31).

* OKR 1: Investing in Product The product focus involves launching three ambient fresh recipes in Q2 2026 with a recipe score target of 4.3. Additionally, the objective includes improving the quality of existing recipes, increasing Direct-to-Consumer (DTOC) add-on net revenue share to over 5%, and optimizing the product selection User Experience (UX) to accommodate increased product choices (00:07:25). Laurent Guillemain also noted that they want to understand the return on investment of adding new recipes (00:09:47).

* Recipe Scoring and Ratings Daniel Arias raised a question about increasing the recipe rating rate in addition to the recipe scores (00:09:47). Laurent Guillemain acknowledged the current response rate of about a hundred per week is low and that the method for collecting data is ad hoc. They agreed to follow up, as they believe the team should challenge themself to collect more and better data, potentially by optimizing the rating entry points within the digital experience and reviewing the multiple

* [EW] Q1 Quarterly Planning Offsite

   * This is a new ritual being introduced to formalize the quarterly roadmaps

   * Goals:

      * Review what was delivered in the previous quarter

      * Discuss and reflect on the key learnings from the previous quarter

      * Share out high-level goals and roadmaps for the new quarter

   * Input needed:

      * Mega Alliance Tribe-Level Update Template (Latest Update: 12.DEC.2025)

      * Q1-2026 Planning Offsite Slides Template

   * Agenda: Q1-2025 GCF Planning Offsite | Agenda & Preparations

* [EW] Quarterly Squad Goals

   * Going forward, we'll use the quarterly planning offsite as an opportunity to formalize any changes to squad KPIs

   * Before the planning workshop, each squad's PM should update CMA Quarterly Squad Goals 2026 for the upcoming quarter, including:

      * Their squad's KPI

      * A goal for the quarter

   * In the "Key Learnings" section of the Tribe Quarterly Update, the tribe lead should explain the rationale for any changes to squad KPIs

   * For avoidance of doubt, the quarterly goal isn't a binding commitment. Neither teams nor individuals will be evaluated based on whether they hit the goal listed in the sheet. We simply want squads to start building a muscle of using KPIs to steer product decision-making, which includes setting ambitious but achievable targets for how much they can move their KPIs

* [Sergei] Recipe Import grows every day (congrats!), but the majority of imported receipts are sourced from HF itself ‚Äî what do we think?

Directions to wrap-up 2025 OKRs

1. Update the 2025 OKR management tool with status and comments for December (columns AP and AQ).

2. All KRs must be updated and reflect one of the 4 final statuses: Done, Done Late, Do Not Meet (including KRs for which targets were only partially achieved - i.e. yellow, red), or Canceled. 

3. Do Not Meet and Canceled KRs must include a comment indicating the reason for not completing them. KRs expected to be completed in 2026 should be moved to Do Not Meet.

For the KRs marked Do Not Meet or Canceled in December, please also explicitly state -

* Whether any work was delivered

* Whether the work is reusable

* If the KR is planned for completion in 2026, please specify this clearly

   * How do you feel about the way planning was done in your previous tribe?

      * What worked well?

         * Shared priorities across squads to avoid conflicts

         * Regular syncs to discuss hot debates and make decisions

         * Define overarching priorities

         * Set a specific goal up front, play with scope later

      * What didn‚Äôt work well?

         * Capacity planning was very granular

         * Did capacity planning for the whole quarter, but then priorities shifted and we didn‚Äôt follow the plan

         * Working on too many things in parallel

         * Dependency mapping - spent time on it upfront, then had to negotiate again during the quarter because priorities changed

### DOC: Debrief: Sree Rangavazzula - Staff Engineer  - 2026/01/06 09:00 EST - Notes by Gemini
ID: 1CDimIAbnh6jonm6Wg18KQT2Iw3COJSuotEBvxte8oO4
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1CDimIAbnh6jonm6Wg18KQT2Iw3COJSuotEBvxte8oO4/edit?usp=drivesdk

Ôªøüìù Notes

Jan 6, 2026

Debrief: Sree Rangavazzula - Staff Engineer 

Invited Nikita Gorshkov Ryan Taylor Inaara Visram Donna Curran Daniel Arias Federico Bertolini Pantelis Chatzinikolis

Attachments Debrief: Sree Rangavazzula - Staff Engineer  

Meeting records Transcript 





Summary

The meeting, attended by Inaara Visram, Nikita Gorshkov, Ryan Taylor, Daniel Arias, and Pantelis Chatzinikolis, was held to review the candidacy of Shri. Ryan Taylor reported that Shri's live coding interview performance was poor, highlighted by a struggle to write basic code and an explicit, uncommunicated reliance on an LLM, which Shri was unable to effectively debug or adapt. Daniel Arias, Nikita Gorshkov, and Pantelis Chatzinikolis agreed that although Shri demonstrated some knowledge of higher-level system architecture, the inability to produce a working solution or explain the LLM-generated code was a major red flag for a staff role requiring direct coding and guidance of junior engineers, leading to a consensus to pass on the candidate.





Details

Notes Length: Standard

* Initial Meeting Setup and Candidate Overview The meeting, attended by Inaara Visram, Nikita Gorshkov, Ryan Taylor, Daniel Arias, and later Pantelis Chatzinikolis, was convened to discuss candidate Shri, with Yed being absent. Inaara Visram asked attendees to recall their interviews, which occurred before the holiday season. The discussion began with Ryan Taylor, who conducted the live coding interview (00:00:00).

* Live Coding Interview Feedback Ryan Taylor reported that while the initial discussion with Shri was fine and they seemed knowledgeable, it was noted that Shri appeared to be distant from writing code, mainly performing code reviews. The subsequent coding challenge was described as one of the worst Ryan Taylor had experienced (00:00:53). Although Shri seemed to understand the requirements, their attempt to write code was "rough," including missing basic logical elements like handling multiple items in a shopping cart. Ryan Taylor speculated that nervousness might have played a role in the struggle (00:02:13).

* Use of LLMs in Coding Challenge A significant issue raised by Ryan Taylor was Shri's explicit use of an LLM during the coding challenge. Shri pasted the question into an LLM and copied the generated code into the interview window without any verbal communication (00:02:13). The code was clearly identifiable as LLM-generated due to its style, comments explaining the LLM's logic, and a flag from Hacker Rank indicating external pasting. Despite using the LLM multiple times, Shri was unable to massage the provided code into a working solution or debug the generated code effectively (00:03:26) (00:06:02).

* Technical Performance and Role Expectations Ryan Taylor concluded that Shri‚Äôs overall technical performance was below the expectation for a staff role, especially since the coding question was technically simple and focused on problem-solving (00:04:25). Daniel Arias confirmed that while they want people to use tools, the expectation is for the candidate to explain their understanding and ideally use pseudo-code before generating code with AI. ### DOC: Discount Communication Presets
ID: 1M8e08SHNq_Z2Q7V45Kasfsv1uP8sPaaz000BRIB7dRo
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1M8e08SHNq_Z2Q7V45Kasfsv1uP8sPaaz000BRIB7dRo/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøDiscount Communication Presets

Contributors: Ipek KalenderAnastasiya BelkinaShay Ben Yacov

Context

Discount communication presets are predefined fields that allow marketing teams to display discount-related messages or offers on various parts of the website. These presets control the content that appears at key customer touchpoints, located on pages such as Landing Pages, Plans Page, Checkout, Reactivation pages.

Marketing Teams can customize the discount messages based on the field presets e.g. Team can decide to display Free Dessert for Life for some users and Free Snacks for life for others. Each preset field controls specific touchpoints on the site, ensuring a consistent and clear message to customers across the user journey.

Touchpoints itself are owned by different product teams, who manage the placement and configuration of the fields, while marketing handles the content. 

All touchpoints integrated with Communication Presets are listed in documentation.

Governance Process for Adding New Discount Communication Touchpoints

The ownership of discount communication is spread across multiple teams product teams own the touchpoints, while marketing teams handle the benefit communication. This requires teams to be aligned on all available fields. Whenever a new field is introduced, it is critical that the team responsible for that section ensures alignment with marketing.

Notification when new field is added

1. Notification to Marketing & Product Teams via Slack

Each time a team plans to add a new discount communication field, they are required to send a message in a dedicated Slack channel (e.g., #discount-communications-updates). This notification will contain the following information:

Slack Message Template:

* Subject: New Discount Communication Touchpoint Field

* Team: [Insert team name]

* Brand: [Insert Brand (All/ HelloFresh/RTE/Mealkit]

* Field Details:

   * Field Name: [e.g., Discount_Slogan]

   * Field Description: [Briefly describe the purpose and content of the field, e.g., "A promotional slogan displayed on the landing page."]

   * Touchpoint Location: [Specify the page and exact location, e.g., "Landing Page - Banner Section."]

   * Content Guidelines (if applicable): [Any limitations, e.g., "Max 50 characters; no special characters."]

   * Link to Documentation: [Link to the updated internal documentation, which should include a screenshot of where the touchpoint is located on the website.]

* Planned day of Roll Out: [e.g., 23-Sep]

* Expectations from Marketing: [e.g., for this field to be filled out for all Activation presets that are in use]

2. Confirmation 

Upon posting in Slack, P&D Teams must confirm receipt of the message and ensure they:

* Understand the new field‚Äôs purpose and placement.

* Have coordinated and finalized updating marketing strategies/content to include the new touchpoint.

* Acknowledge any guidelines, limitations, or formatting rules.

[!] Please wait until both 1 POC from both NA and International P&D to confirm they are aligned with the changes.

3. Documentation Update

Update the documentation for the new field. Documentation must include:

* Field name and description

* Page(s) and sections where the touchpoint is active

* A screenshot or visual aid highlighting where the new touchpoint is located.

* Usage guidelines, including length, format, and content rules

* Clear directions on how marketing can use the new field

4. How to implement a new field

To introduce a new field into discount communication configuration (to be able to use it in CUI) a new Pull

### DOC: Discovery: How to onboard markets with multiple product families into price sets
ID: 1kOT8uEq4iINM_l6sh57o_fo-2V4ojlcTFfly79OM34U
Link: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1kOT8uEq4iINM_l6sh57o_fo-2V4ojlcTFfly79OM34U/edit?usp=drivesdk
----------------------------------------

ÔªøProposal

Goal        1

Status Quo        2

Limitation in CUI        2

Adopting Size-Based Price Sets        3

Use Case 1: Shared Sizes and Prices Across Different Product Categories        4

Price Set Creation        4

Use Case 3: Markets Offering Multiple Product Categories with Different Pricing        6

Price Set Creation        7

Price Experiment Setup        9

Price Set Groups        10

Price Set Group Constraints        11

Project Plan: Onboarding Markets with Multiple Product Families into Price Sets        12

Phase 1: Enable Multi-Product-Category Price Set Creation (Use Case 1 & 2)        13

Phase 2: Introduce Price Set Groups and Experiment Integration (Use Case 3)        13

Phase 3: Decouple Prices from Product Handles (Long-Term Target Architecture)        14

Goal

The objective of this document is to outline the strategy for onboarding markets that offer multiple product families onto the Price Sets technology. This technology is crucial because it allows for rapid price experimentation without the need to duplicate product families.





Status Quo

Price Sets have been deployed in most markets that currently only offer the "classic-box" subscription. Progress on this initiative can be tracked via the rollout plan.

The existing version of Price Sets is built upon the legacy product price data model, which directly links prices to specific product handles.

Limitation in CUI

Currently, the Price Set management tool within CUI (Customer User Interface) is restricted to creating Price Sets solely for the classic-box-unified product family. Users do not have the option to select other product families, nor can they select multiple families.

See an example of a price set in CUI: https://cui.hellofresh.io/price-experimentation/price-set-management/c2779461-927c-480f-a3f3-0d5c05e77b43/view   

Long-Term Target Architecture 

The Long-Term Target Architecture aims to fundamentally decouple price sets from individual product handles (e.g., US-CBU-3-2-0).





Instead, the pricing will be driven by a Size-Based Price Set model, where a price set functions purely as a reusable price list based on the core plan dimensions: Number of Meals X Number of People.

Key Principles of the Target Architecture

* Decoupling from Product Handles: Price sets will no longer be directly associated with, or contain, specific product handle IDs.

* Size-Based Definition: A price set will define the price points (Total Price, Shipping Fee, etc.) solely for each unique combination of meals and people (e.g., 3 meals for 2 people, 4 meals for 4 people).

* Reusability: A single price set can be applied across multiple, compatible product categories[a][b] within the same market (e.g., Classic Box and Thermomix Box) provided they share the same price structure and sizes. The price set acts like a template that is applied to a category.

* Simplified Price Experimentation: By abstracting the price from the product handler, price experiments can be designed once and deployed simultaneously across all compatible product categories.





This evolution is a necessary step to simplify management, reduce data redundancy, and enable flexible, rapid price experimentation across ou

New venture leaders often tell us their biggest frustration is making
